<div id="review_2012204021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2012204021" />
    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18656418-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588653801p2/18656418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2012204021?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2012204021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6314431112861011756">4.5 stars <br/><br/>I actually like zombie books and so I've read quite a few. This one definitely rates up there among the top, achieving the goal of situating an interesting story in a post-zombie apocalypse world.The result in this case is a sort of genre mash-up of zombie survival with political thriller, and it works wonderfully. <br/><br/>Grant has a wordy storytelling style, which I first noticed when I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13641105.Parasite__Parasitology___1_' title='Parasite (Parasitology, #1) by Mira Grant' rel='nofollow noopener'>Parasite</a>, but I think she makes it work with the narrative. In both cases the verbosity seems consist</span>
  <span id="freeText6314431112861011756" style="display:none">4.5 stars <br /><br />I actually like zombie books and so I've read quite a few. This one definitely rates up there among the top, achieving the goal of situating an interesting story in a post-zombie apocalypse world.The result in this case is a sort of genre mash-up of zombie survival with political thriller, and it works wonderfully. <br /><br />Grant has a wordy storytelling style, which I first noticed when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13641105.Parasite__Parasitology___1_" title="Parasite (Parasitology, #1) by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Parasite</a>, but I think she makes it work with the narrative. In both cases the verbosity seems consistent with the characters, particularly here, where the main character is a news blogger. The only reason it took me so long to read it was that I listened to Feed as an audiobook. Even though it was very long, I never tired of it; both narrators did a great job. The last 20% of the book in particular is edge-of-your-seat listening.<br /><br />One thing I particularly liked about this book was the relationship between siblings Georgia and Shaun Mason. Instead of a romantic couple, we have a brother and sister who live and work together, who protect each other, and create an emotionally safe environment for themselves in a dangerous world. <br /><br />Definitely a book worth reading if you like the genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6314431112861011756" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=dystopian-apocalyptic">dystopian-apocalyptic</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=given-away">given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=cats">cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171690428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11833935193216016034"><b>A gripping, suspenseful read with lots of heart.</b><br/><br/><b>Feed</b> is by no means a perfect book. It could be considered lengthy. There is way too much info-dumping (although I found the info dumped very interesting!). The blood testing procedure is described in detail about 478 times. Georgia is forced to take off her sunglasses by unfriendly security officers at least every 50 pages. The senator and his wife are a little too nice, whereas the villain is a little too fanatic and easy to spot. It is not that </span>
  <span id="freeText11833935193216016034" style="display:none"><b>A gripping, suspenseful read with lots of heart.</b><br /><br /><b>Feed</b> is by no means a perfect book. It could be considered lengthy. There is way too much info-dumping (although I found the info dumped very interesting!). The blood testing procedure is described in detail about 478 times. Georgia is forced to take off her sunglasses by unfriendly security officers at least every 50 pages. The senator and his wife are a little too nice, whereas the villain is a little too fanatic and easy to spot. It is not that hard to figure out what will happen next after the first incident at the camp. The relationship between Georgia and Shane borders on destructive and is – let’s face it – a little weird. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The cat dies!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Yet, despite its flaws, I loved this book. Not quite enough to give it five stars, but definitely enough to look very much forward to reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8429687.Deadline__Newsflesh_Trilogy__2_" title="Deadline (Newsflesh Trilogy #2) by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadline</a> (which arrived today from Amazon) and to be more than a little devastated by the ending Mira Grant left us with. I shed a few tears. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I am still pissed the cat died. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />If Deadline has one of those evil cliff hangers (I suspect it does), I will be cursing myself for not having waited until the third book in the trilogy was available. <br /><br />I’m finding it hard to recommend <b>Feed</b> to a certain type of reader – probably because my experience with political thrillers/zombie books is rather limited. But I have to say that for me; this book was a welcome change from all the YA I’ve been reading lately. It has definitely inspired me become a more versatile reader again. I feel like I’ve been neglecting everything non-YA in the last two years. I used to love psychological thrillers, crime novels and epic fantasy when I was younger, but have practically been ignoring those genres for quite some time now. Anyways, to stop rambling: Despite the technical approach this book takes – all the talk about blogging, viruses mutating, blood testing, weapons …– it still has lots of heart. Georgia is a very down-to-earth heroine, her narration is far from emotional, but yet, you can always feel her deep love for her brother and the respect she has for her colleagues and friends. She is always observing, always looking for the truth, and terribly honest herself. She has principles and she stands by them no matter what. The banter between her and Shaun is just priceless, but the tender moments were what made me tear up a little. Their brother-sister connection is definitely unique <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and I’m finding it really hard to imagine how the next book will work without it. Georgia and Shaun were so close it is impossible for me to believe that he will be able to cope with her death and move on. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />All in all, <b>I think you might like this book if …</b> (no liability assumed ;))<br /><br /><blockquote>~ you are interested in the way the media influences our lives on one side, but also how journalist live and work on the other.<br /><br />~ you want to know what a sickness can do to our society, how it can make people hole up and hide, how it can take away nearly all of your personal freedoms.<br /><br />~ you are interested in politics and in the way they shape our society, especially in exceptional situations and danger. <br /><br />~ you are a fan of conspiracy theories.<br /><br />~ you don’t mind a lot of technical/medical talk you don’t necessarily understand.<br /><br />~ you can take a certain amount of gore and violence.<br /><br />~ you are not looking for the classical let’s-go-out-and-kill-some-zombies adventure.<br /><br />~ you can live with an absence of romance and swooning ;).</blockquote><br />But, if you are a cat fan like me, a small warning: Don’t get too attached to the cat. It will only bring you misery.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11833935193216016034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_173306448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173306448" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173306448?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173306448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5847420780036596067"><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br/>I’m sorry, I can’t actually read this last page BECAUSE OF THE TEARS. Or at least the metaphorical ones… because I don’t cry at books… but you get what I mean. This book is horrifically sad. <br/><b><br/>High points.</b><br/>ZOMBIES. I am a huge fan of zombies… and I always thought that everyone else was too, but from reading reviews of this a main reason why people were unsure about this was because of the zombies. Zombies were the reason why I picked up these books. More than zombies- even though I </span>
  <span id="freeText5847420780036596067" style="display:none"><b>Initial Thoughts</b><br />I’m sorry, I can’t actually read this last page BECAUSE OF THE TEARS. Or at least the metaphorical ones… because I don’t cry at books… but you get what I mean. This book is horrifically sad. <br /><b><br />High points.</b><br />ZOMBIES. I am a huge fan of zombies… and I always thought that everyone else was too, but from reading reviews of this a main reason why people were unsure about this was because of the zombies. Zombies were the reason why I picked up these books. More than zombies- even though I am all for zombies, they only have a cameo appearance in this story. It is about so much more and it’s a shame that this book is being described as a ‘zombie book’ because there is like a million other things that go on as well. Great depiction of siblings… very realistic but also hilarious and poignant *sob*. The setting- so much thought has gone into this and the back story is amazing. Also… LOVE the fact that variations of George (Romero) are the popular names of the time because that would actually happen. News and journalism- what a fascinating speculation of the future of the news and the rise of the importance blogs… I’m pretty sure Ms Grant saw into the future with that one. Hopefully not about the evil Rising and gnashing zombies though…<br />TENSION. Man, this book was tense I practically have no nails left. Red light green light red light green light red… ARGH. Subtle but effective writing that feeds (sorry… couldn’t think of a better word) little clue snippets into the dialogue so you’re left guessing write up until the end. And speaking of the end…in the great words of Bony M…. oh ma looooord. <br />This book was totally not what I was expecting and it always left me guessing. I don’t mean to sound big headed, but I quite often predict what is going to happen in things…not because they are necessarily flimsy plots, but because I’ve watched a lot of television and read a lot of books. So even though I had some pretty major quibbles with this book, I loved this book so much, not only for having an interesting story, exploring fascinating concepts and ideas but for proving that actually, Jo… you’re not as smart as you think. Because damn, I did NOT expect this book to go the way it did. Flabbergasted. <br /><br /><br /><b>Low points.</b> <br />This book really started off sooooo slow and it took quite a while for things to happen. There was also a lot of politics and even though it was interesting to get the back story and why what was happening was happening, I found it to be unnecessarily in depth and it became quite repetitive. I understand that it was important for the reader to get understand the big ideas (especially when you read Deadline, the second book of the trilogy)… but it did become a bit tedious. The blogging/technical side of things. Gosh there was a lot of technical jargon in this book (which is probably a high point for a lot of people, but I am a geek but not a computer geek) and a lot of it went over my head. This is probably my fault for my eyes glazing over whenever big bro tried to explain computer things to me… but about 60% of this was lost on my poor English Literature/Film Studying brain. <br />I loved Georgia as a character- she is intelligent, resourceful, dedicated to her profession and the search for truth and she’s caring but she’s not a simpering girly girl, which was great because I don’t think I could have handled romangst in this book. BUT… I really didn’t like her as a narrator. I like to connect with my narrators and I’m not saying George was heartless or anything, but… I think the only thing I had in common with her is how I take my caffeine: Cold. <br /><br /><b>Heroine/Hero/ Best friend. </b><br />I briefly mentioned George in the low points section… so I won’t go on too much about her. I’ll focus on my positive feelings towards her. I thought she was such an original character… a girl who runs a blog documenting the world post- zombie rising, who surpasses all the boys with her mad computer skills and can kill zombies? YES PLEASE. And also, she’s a writer looking for the truth. Aren’t we all, George? Aren’t we all? <br />What I loved about her was that even though George is a complete tom boy and perhaps the furthest away from loving material things as you can get (except for the hair dye, of course!)… she wasn’t really aggressive with it. She is different than all the other girls but she accepts this and just gets on with it and gets on with her job. I’m so glad that Grant wasn’t like ‘LOOK HOW ORIGINAL THIS TOMBOY CHARACTER WHO DOESN’T LIKE FASHIONABLE CLOTHES AND DOESN’T UNDERSTAND BOYS IS’ all the time, because in a lot of dystopian novels (*cough* Mockingjay *cough*) this happens and it’s so off-putting and amazing characters (*cough* Mockingjay *cough*) are ruined by this.<br />Even though I didn’t have much in common with George and didn’t relate to her as much as I have narrators in other books I’ve read… I appreciated that it was her telling the story because in hindsight (which, of course, is 20:20) I don’t think this book would have worked if it hadn’t been told from how she saw it from behind her aviators. <br />Which leads me nicely to Shaun (and yes, I immediately thought of <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1vUfBOdSmBU" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and <a href="http://www.best-horror-movies.com/images/shaun-of-the-dead-trio.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a>) but no offense to Simon Pegg, who does have some kind of nerdy British charm and an understandable fondness for Cornettos… this Shaun was muuuuuuch cuter and yes, I have a crush on him. He is George’s brother, co-worker and best friend. But unlike George, he's kinda glad there are zombies everywhere because his job is to go into the field and report on the zombies from up-close. And, of course, poke them with sticks. <br />Shaun is such a great character: he’s hilarious, he’s stupid, he’s a typical boy, he's dangerous, he walks around in his underwear (BOOM.), he’s reckless but he has such a good heart and he's so honorable and just a massive cutie in cargo pants. <br />I also love the relationship between George and Shaun, it’s such an interesting dynamic because normally with sibling relationships in books it seems so forced and ‘Ohh my brother/sister is soo annoying’. But G &amp; S really care for each other, they rib each other but they seem to slot perfectly together, their relationship was my favourite part of this book. Sigh. <br /><b><br />Baddie.</b><br />Ignoring the fact that the flesh-eating zombies are kinda baddies… I was a little disappointed with the main, main baddie. I like my evil characters with a bit of mystery and intrigue but this one seemed to just stroll up on the page and be like ‘HI JO, I’M EVIL AND I’M GOING TO CAUSE PROBLEMS. MUHAHAHA’ as he twiddled his moustache. BUT BUT… I’m writing this book after I read Deadline and like I said about hindsight being great, even though the baddie in Feed wasn't the best…Grant did an amazing job at setting up the baddies for book numero deux. The bigger picture ‘n’ all. <br /><b><br />Theme Tune.</b><br /><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_e0Ju4eDROE&amp;feature=player_embedded" rel="nofollow noopener">They Are Night Zombies!- Sufjan Stevens.</a><br /><br />I was going to choose a very literal song for this book… but I decided against it when I found this gem by Sufjan Stevens. When I first saw the title, I was expecting it to be a funny song and then was surprised at the sense of melancholy, the lack of permanence and the poignancy that it evoked. Like how I felt with this book, when my preconceptions were challenged. The song is all about the resurrection and how the mistakes of the past can shape the future which makes it particularly relevant to the message of the book. Also… it has possibly the best title ever. (The full title is “They are Night Zombies! They are Neighbours! They Have Come Back from the Dead! Aaaah”)<br /><br /><b>Angst Level.</b><br />10/10. GOD. This book. I finished this book a few days ago but I literally couldn’t bring myself to write about it because the ending shocked me and affected me so much. I keep thinking about it and nearly drown in the emotion that it brings. There are a lot of deaths in this book, some are pretty obvious and easily to predict, but they are dealt with such raw emotion that even though you may have guessed it was coming, you still feel your heart ripped out and mourn with the characters.<br /><br /><b><br />Recommended For.</b><br />People who think zombies are better than unicorns. People who like adventure books. People who like dystopian books that have a bit more ‘ooomph’ to them. People who don’t mind their stories lacking in romance. People who like strong, original and unflappable female narrators. People who are interested in journalism and the way news is presented. People who like conspiracies. People who are scientifically inclined. People who saw 28 Days Later and thought “I want to go to there”. People who believe in exposing the truth, no matter what. People who have a brother/sister. People who would quite happily tolerate their boyfriend poking rabid dead people with sticks because he’s super cute. People who have nerves of steel. People who have no tear ducts and/or emotions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5847420780036596067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_513219544" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513219544" />
    <a title="Alisha-Dear Constant Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader"><img alt="Alisha-Dear Constant Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368036120p2/2463184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513219544?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisha-Dear Constant Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisha-Dear Constant Reader" href="/user/show/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader">Alisha-Dear Constant Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader?shelf=slooooow">slooooow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader?shelf=complete-let-down">complete-let-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader?shelf=dumber-for-having-read">dumber-for-having-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader?shelf=dumb-plot-lines">dumb-plot-lines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader?shelf=mysteries-abound">mysteries-abound</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2463184-alisha-dear-constant-reader?shelf=political-intrigue">political-intrigue</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513219544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6637621472166306860"><b>So dumb: An Angry Analysis</b> <br/><br/>And my final conclusion for this book is...<br/><br/><a href='http://s57.beta.photobucket.com/user/alishaccunningham/media/thumbsdown_zps8a996815.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406172ra/792100.gif' alt=' photo thumbsdown_zps8a996815.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><blockquote>Here's why I eye-rolled myself into a headache while reading <b>Feed</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Here we are, 28 years into the future and the blogging world is the shit! The world has turned to blogs for their reliable truth after the zombie apocalypse. Please tell me why I don't have to explain how dumb that is? Fine. Not a big deal? Okay.<br/><br/>The bloggers have broken themselves down into three categories:<br/><br/>Newsies--Yes, as in from the ancient movie of the s</span>
  <span id="freeText6637621472166306860" style="display:none"><b>So dumb: An Angry Analysis</b> <br><br>And my final conclusion for this book is...<br><br><a href="http://s57.beta.photobucket.com/user/alishaccunningham/media/thumbsdown_zps8a996815.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406172ra/792100.gif" alt=" photo thumbsdown_zps8a996815.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><blockquote>Here's why I eye-rolled myself into a headache while reading <b>Feed</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Here we are, 28 years into the future and the blogging world is the shit! The world has turned to blogs for their reliable truth after the zombie apocalypse. Please tell me why I don't have to explain how dumb that is? Fine. Not a big deal? Okay.<br><br>The bloggers have broken themselves down into three categories:<br><br>Newsies--Yes, as in from the ancient movie of the same title. These folks are straight reporters.<br><br>Irwins--As in Steve Irwin. These are the action/dare devil reporters. Oh for fuck's sake! It's 28 years into the future, Irwin has been dead now for how many years? But no, we're Irwins!<br><br>Fictionals--See bad stories and worse poems.<br><br>While I'm raging about pop-culture, which seems to have stalled out in this book at 2001, how the hell do we have Newsies and Irwins and nobody's heard of <i>Buffy the Vampire Slayer?</i> M'Kay. Sure.<br><br><br>The technology seems to have stalled out around the early 2000s as well. Apparently, Georgia needs three cell phones--er, why? Also, why the fuck do I need to know this? Lots of dumb details really weigh the story down.<br><br>That was annoying, but more annoying were the pages worth of the setting up of the technology. Dear, Lord! I don't give a flying fuck why you connected this to that, or the other. I don't need to read more pages about Buffy fixing this and wires being connected. No! You are wasting my time!<br><br>Oh, and don't get me started on the finger pricking blood tests! Apparently they have to hurt because the pain is psychological BARLB WHMOLUM. <b>SCIENCE!</b> <br><br>So, consumers <i>don't</i> want a blood scanner that doesn't hurt? You know, because they <i>NEVER</i> have to scan? Oh, wait! They do have to scan? Like ever other page? Oh. So why the fuck does it have to hurt and prick every fucking finger? GARBLE BLARB, SCIENCE!<br><br><br><br><b>Meanwhile in politics...this boring shit happened.</b><br><br>Yes, <b>Feed</b> is far more about the politics of the future than anything else--especially zombies. Surprise, fuckers! This zombie book is not about zombies! We get to hear all about the state of the union from George, who is the most cliche, unlikeable, hypocritical character ever! <br><br><b>George and why I hate her:</b><br><br>Wears nondescript black clothing with lots of pockets and boots<br><br>Doesn't like touching or affection of any kind<br><br>Does not like animals<br><br>Has a strange relationship with adopted brother<br><br>Believes that showing emotion is weak<br><br>Is an egocentric asshole who likes the sound of her own voice<br><br>Loves to power play everyone, including her employees<br><br><a href="http://s57.beta.photobucket.com/user/alishaccunningham/media/tumblr_inline_mghn6yv72l1rwcy4q_zps5fe5043f.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406172ra/792101.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_mghn6yv72l1rwcy4q_zps5fe5043f.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Grant writes George these horrible blog posts about her musings about the world. They suck! First, there's WAY too many of them. Second, they all start to blend together. Third, and this is 450 pages later, I began to realize that Grant is most likely the kind of person who loves the sound of her own voice. Oh, the self-important blathering! <br><br>Overall, this book is awful for all kinds of reasons! It's way too fucking long, the characters are completely without merit, and the story suuuukkkkxxx! Once I realized who the bad guy was, I was so done. Who wants to keep reading self-important BLAR BARL BLARB when you know who the cliche bad guy is. Can you say, President Snow, much? <br><br><b>Feed</b> feels very much as though it were written ten years ago, or more. The pop culture references were terrible and could have been solved by changing the stupid terminology, or just not making the damn book set SO freaking far into the future. Newsies and Irwins? I about gagged. How dumb. <br><br>But here's the thing about dumb. I can suspend disbelief even for dumb if the characters and story work, but they didn't. George is awful and the plot is so predictable it actually made my head hurt. The world building was good, but honestly, a world without a plot is just a world.<br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6637621472166306860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CjTwz0UN3pOxnWBIQvvq6Mid2/DRta86kPqZinhUxHYwEpkd/lMX+xa21Cm1DuA3HsI8OB84IV3LhN87tRc27A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dn2bIH4F/l53wIVhLn/eFsVP9JdA4KTgeN8DDRvi28BMW/LyxVs3NtDrMQDZitTJExATX45tKocjoUW81qEpWg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer1664551762759414829">Mira also writes as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2860219.Seanan_McGuire' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seanan McGuire</a>.<br/><br/>Born and raised in Northern California, Mira Grant has made a lifelong study of horror movies, horrible viruses, and the inevitable threat of the living dead. In college, she was voted Most Likely to Summon Something Horrible in the Cornfield, and was a founding member of the Horror Movie Sleep-Away Survival Camp, where her record for time survived in the Swamp C</span>
  <span id="freeText1664551762759414829" style="display:none">Mira also writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2860219.Seanan_McGuire" rel="nofollow noopener">Seanan McGuire</a>.<br /><br />Born and raised in Northern California, Mira Grant has made a lifelong study of horror movies, horrible viruses, and the inevitable threat of the living dead. In college, she was voted Most Likely to Summon Something Horrible in the Cornfield, and was a founding member of the Horror Movie Sleep-Away Survival Camp, where her record for time survived in the Swamp Cannibals scenario remains unchallenged.<br /><br />Mira lives in a crumbling farmhouse with an assortment of cats, horror movies, comics, and books about horrible diseases. When not writing, she splits her time between travel, auditing college virology courses, and watching more horror movies than is strictly good for you. Favorite vacation spots include Seattle, London, and a large haunted corn maze just outside of Huntsville, Alabama.<br /><br />Mira sleeps with a machete under her bed, and highly suggests that you do the same.<br /><br /></span>
